diag.Summary)\n79: \n80: \tappendSourceSnippets(&buf, diag, color)\n81: \n82: \tif diag.Detail != \"\" {\n83: \t\tparaWidth := width - leftRuleWidth - 1 // leave room for the left rule\n84: \t\tif paraWidth > 0 {\n85: \t\t\tlines := strings.Split(diag.Detail, \"\\n\")\n86: \t\t\tfor _, line := range lines {\n87: \t\t\t\tif !strings.HasPrefix(line, \" \") {\n88: \t\t\t\t\tline = wordwrap.WrapString(line, uint(paraWidth))\n89: \t\t\t\t}\n90: \t\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s\\n\", line)\n91: \t\t\t}\n92: \t\t} else {\n93: \t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s\\n\", diag.Detail)\n94: \t\t}\n95: \t}\n96: \n97: \t// Before we return, we'll finally add the left rule prefixes to each\n98: \t// line so that the overall message is visually delimited from what's\n99: \t// around it. We'll do that by scanning over what we already generated\n100: \t// and adding the prefix for each line.\n101: \tvar ruleBuf strings.Builder\n102: \tsc := bufio.NewScanner(&buf)\n103: \truleBuf.WriteString(leftRuleStart)\n104: \truleBuf.WriteByte('\\n')\n105: \tfor sc.Scan() {\n106: \t\tline := sc.Text()\n107: \t\tprefix := leftRuleLine\n108: \t\tif line == \"\" {\n109: \t\t\t// Don't print the space after the line if there would be nothing\n110: \t\t\t// after it anyway.\n111: \t\t\tprefix = strings.TrimSpace(prefix)\n112: \t\t}\n113: \t\truleBuf.WriteString(prefix)\n114: \t\truleBuf.WriteString(line)\n115: \t\truleBuf.WriteByte('\\n')\n116: \t}\n117: \truleBuf.WriteString(leftRuleEnd)\n118: \truleBuf.WriteByte('\\n')\n119: \n120: \treturn ruleBuf.String()\n121: }\n122: \n123: // DiagnosticPlain is an alternative to Diagnostic which minimises the use of\n124: // virtual terminal formatting sequences.\n125: //\n126: // It is intended for use in automation and other contexts in which diagnostic\n127: // messages are parsed from the Terraform output.\n128: func DiagnosticPlain(diag tfdiags.Diagnostic, sources map[string][]byte, width int) string {\n129: \treturn DiagnosticPlainFromJSON(viewsjson.NewDiagnostic(diag, sources), width)\n130: }\n131: \n132: func DiagnosticPlainFromJSON(diag *viewsjson.Diagnostic, width int) string {\n133: \tif diag == nil {\n134: \t\t// No good reason to pass a nil diagnostic in here...\n135: \t\treturn \"\"\n136: \t}\n137: \n138: \tvar buf bytes.Buffer\n139: \n140: \tswitch diag.Severity {\n141: \tcase viewsjson.DiagnosticSeverityError:\n142: \t\tbuf.WriteString(\"\\nError: \")\n143: \tcase viewsjson.DiagnosticSeverityWarning:\n144: \t\tbuf.WriteString(\"\\nWarning: \")\n145: \tdefault:\n146: \t\tbuf.WriteString(\"\\n\")\n147: \t}\n148: \n149: \t// We don't wrap the summary, since we expect it to be terse, and since\n150: \t// this is where we put the text of a native Go error it may not always\n151: \t// be pure text that lends itself well to word-wrapping.\n152: \tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s\\n\\n\", diag.Summary)\n153: \n154: \tappendSourceSnippets(&buf, diag, disabledColorize)\n155: \n156: \tif diag.Detail != \"\" {\n157: \t\tif width > 1 {\n158: \t\t\tlines := strings.Split(diag.Detail, \"\\n\")\n159: \t\t\tfor _, line := range lines {\n160: \t\t\t\tif !strings.HasPrefix(line, \" \") {\n161: \t\t\t\t\tline = wordwrap.WrapString(line, uint(width-1))\n162: \t\t\t\t}\n163: \t\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s\\n\", line)\n164: \t\t\t}\n165: \t\t} else {\n166: \t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s\\n\", diag.Detail)\n167: \t\t}\n168: \t}\n169: \n170: \treturn buf.String()\n171: }\n172: \n173: // DiagnosticWarningsCompact is an alternative to Diagnostic for when all of\n174: // the given diagnostics are warnings and we want to show them compactly,\n175: // with only two lines per warning and excluding all of the detail information.\n176: //\n177: // The caller may optionally pre-process the given diagnostics with\n178: // ConsolidateWarnings, in which case this function will recognize consolidated\n179: // messages and include an indication that they are consolidated.\n180: //\n181: // Do not pass non-warning diagnostics to this function, or the result will\n182: // be nonsense.\n183: func DiagnosticWarningsCompact(diags tfdiags.Diagnostics, color *colorstring.Colorize) string {\n184: \tvar b strings.Builder\n185: \tb.WriteString(color.Color(\"[bold][yellow]Warnings:[reset]\\n\\n\"))\n186: \tfor _, diag := range diags {\n187: \t\tsources := tfdiags.WarningGroupSourceRanges(diag)\n188: \t\tb.WriteString(fmt.Sprintf(\"- %s\\n\", diag.Description().Summary))\n189: \t\tif len(sources) > 0 {\n190: \t\t\tmainSource := sources[0]\n191: \t\t\tif mainSource.Subject != nil {\n192: \t\t\t\tif len(sources) > 1 {\n193: \t\t\t\t\tb.WriteString(fmt.Sprintf(\n194: \t\t\t\t\t\t\"  on %s line %d (and %d more)\\n\",\n195: \t\t\t\t\t\tmainSource.Subject.Filename,\n196: \t\t\t\t\t\tmainSource.Subject.Start.Line,\n197: \t\t\t\t\t\tlen(sources)-1,\n198: \t\t\t\t\t))\n199: \t\t\t\t} else {\n200: \t\t\t\t\tb.WriteString(fmt.Sprintf(\n201: \t\t\t\t\t\t\"  on %s line %d\\n\",\n202: \t\t\t\t\t\tmainSource.Subject.Filename,\n203: \t\t\t\t\t\tmainSource.Subject.Start.Line,\n204: \t\t\t\t\t))\n205: \t\t\t\t}\n206: \t\t\t} else if len(sources) > 1 {\n207: \t\t\t\tb.WriteString(fmt.Sprintf(\n208: \t\t\t\t\t\"  (%d occurences of this warning)\\n\",\n209: \t\t\t\t\tlen(sources),\n210: \t\t\t\t))\n211: \t\t\t}\n212: \t\t}\n213: \t}\n214: \n215: \treturn b.String()\n216: }\n217: \n218: func appendSourceSnippets(buf *bytes.Buffer, diag *viewsjson.Diagnostic, color *colorstring.Colorize) {\n219: \tif diag.Address != \"\" {\n220: \t\tfmt.Fprintf(buf, \"  with %s,\\n\", diag.Address)\n221: \t}\n222: \n223: \tif diag.Range == nil {\n224: \t\treturn\n225: \t}\n226: \n227: \tif diag.Snippet == nil {\n228: \t\t// This should generally not happen, as long as sources are always\n229: \t\t// loaded through the main loader. We may load things in other\n230: \t\t// ways in weird cases, so we'll tolerate it at the expense of\n231: \t\t// a not-so-helpful error message.\n232: \t\tfmt.Fprintf(buf, \"  on %s line %d:\\n  (source code not available)\\n\", diag.Range.Filename, diag.Range.Start.Line)\n233: \t} else {\n234: \t\tsnippet := diag.Snippet\n235: \t\tcode := snippet.Code\n236: \n237: \t\tvar contextStr diag.Range.Start.Line, contextStr)\n242: \n243: \t\t// Split the snippet and render the highlighted section with underlines\n244: \t\tstart := snippet.HighlightStartOffset\n245: \t\tend := snippet.HighlightEndOffset\n246: \n247: \t\t// Only buggy diagnostics can have an end range before the start, but\n248: \t\t// we need to ensure we don't crash here if that happens.\n249: \t\tif end < start {\n250: \t\t\tend = start + 1\n251: \t\t\tif end > len(code) {\n252: \t\t\t\tend = len(code)\n253: \t\t\t}\n254: \t\t}\n255: \n256: \t\t// If either start or end is out of range for the code buffer then\n257: \t\t// we'll cap them at the bounds just to avoid a panic, although\n258: \t\t// this would happen only if there's a bug in the code generating\n259: \t\t// the snippet objects.\n260: \t\tif start < 0 {\n261: \t\t\tstart = 0\n262: \t\t} else if start > len(code) {\n263: \t\t\tstart = len(code)\n264: \t\t}\n265: \t\tif end < 0 {\n266: \t\t\tend = 0\n267: \t\t} else if end > len(code) {\n268: \t\t\tend = len(code)\n269: \t\t}\n270: \n271: \t\tbefore, highlight, after := code[0:start], code[start:end], code[end:]\n272: \t\tcode = fmt.Sprintf(color.Color(\"%s[underline]%s[reset]%s\"), before, highlight, after)\n273: \n274: \t\t// Split the snippet into lines and render one at a time\n275: \t\tlines := strings.Split(code, \n284: \t\tif len(snippet.Values) > 0 || (snippet.FunctionCall != nil && snippet.FunctionCall.Signature != nil) {\n285: \t\t\t// The diagnostic may also have information about the dynamic\n286: \t\t\t// values of relevant variables at the point of evaluation.\n287: \t\t\t// This is particularly useful for expressions that get evaluated\n288: \t\t\t// multiple times with different values, \t\t\tcopy(values, snippet.Values)\n292: \t\t\tsort.Slice(values, func(i, j int) bool {\n293: \t\t\t\treturn values[i].Traversal < values[j].Traversal\n294: \t\t\t})\n295: \n296: \t\t\tfmt.Fprint(buf, \t\t\t\t\t\tbuf.WriteString(\", \")\n303: \t\t\t\t\t}\n304: \t\t\t\t\tbuf.WriteString(param.Name)\n305: \t\t\t\t}\n306: \t\t\t\tif param := callInfo.Signature.VariadicParam; param != nil {\n307: The described changes\\n25: // are not applied directly, but contain an approximation of the final\\n26: // result that will be completed during apply by resolving any values that\\n27: // cannot be predicted.\\n28: //\\n29: // A plan must always be accompanied by the configuration it was built from,\\n30: // since the plan does not itself include all of the information required to\\n31: // make the changes indicated.\\n32: type Plan struct {\\n33: \\t// Mode is the mode under which this plan was created.\\n34: \\t//\\n35: \\t// This is only recorded to allow for UI differences when presenting plans\\n36: \\t// to the end-user, and so it must not be used to influence apply-time\\n37: \\t// behavior. New behavior\\n42: \\t// should not be added based on this flag, and changing the flag should be\\n43: \\t// checked carefully against existing destroy behaviors.\\n44: \\tUIMode Mode\\n45: \\n46: \\t// VariableValues, VariableMarks, and ApplyTimeVariables together describe\\n47: \\t// how Terraform should decide the input variable values for the apply\\n48: \\t// phase if this plan is to be applied.\\n49: \\t//\\n50: \\t// VariableValues and VariableMarks describe persisted (non-ephemeral)\\n51: \\t// values that were set as part of the planning options and are to be\\n52: \\t// re-used during the apply phase. VariableValues can potentially contain\\n53: \\t// unknown values for a speculative plan, but the variable values must\\n54: \\t// all be known for a plan that will subsequently be applied.\\n55: \\t//\\n56: \\t// ApplyTimeVariables retains the names of any ephemeral variables that were\\n57: \\t// set (non-null) during the planning phase and must therefore be\\n58: \\t// re-supplied by the caller (potentially with different values) during\\n59: \\t// the apply phase. Ephemeral input variables are intended for populating\\n60: \\t// arguments for other ephemeral objects in the configuration, such as\\n61: \\t// provider configurations. Although the values for these variables can\\n62: \\t// change between plan and apply, their \\\"nullness\\\" may not.\\n63: \\tVariableValues     map[string]DynamicValue\\n64: \\tVariableMarks      map[string][]cty.PathValueMarks\\n65: \\tApplyTimeVariables collections.Set[string]\\n66: \\n67: \\tChanges           *ChangesSrc\\n68: \\tDriftedResources  []*ResourceInstanceChangeSrc\\n69: \\tDeferredResources []*DeferredResourceInstanceChangeSrc\\n70: \\tTargetAddrs       []addrs.Targetable\\n71: \\tForceReplaceAddrs []addrs.AbsResourceInstance\\n72: \\tBackend           Backend\\n73: \\n74: \\t// Complete is true if Terraform considers this to be a \\\"complete\\\" plan,\\n75: \\t// which is to say that it includes a planned action (even if no-op)\\n76: \\t// for every resource instance object that was mentioned across both\\n77: \\t// the desired state and prior state.\\n78: \\t//\\n79: \\t// If Complete is false then the plan might still be applyable (check\\n80: \\t// [Plan.Applyable]) but after applying it the operator should be reminded\\n81: \\t// to plan and apply again to hopefully make more progress towards\\n82: \\t// convergence.\\n83: \\t//\\n84: \\t// For an incomplete plan, other fields of this type may give more context\\n85: \\t// about why the plan is incomplete, which a UI layer could present to\\n86: \\t// the user as part of a warning that the plan is incomplete.\\n87: \\tComplete bool\\n88: \\n89: \\t// Applyable is true if both Terraform was able to create a plan\\n90: \\t// successfully and if the plan calls for making some sort of meaningful\\n91: \\t// change.\\n92: \\t//\\n93: \\t// If [Plan.Errored] is also set then that means the plan is non-applyable\\n94: \\t// due to an error. If not then the plan was created successfully but found\\n95: \\t// no material differences between desired and prior state, and so\\n96: \\t// applying this plan would achieve nothing.\\n97: \\tApplyable bool\\n98: \\n99: \\t// Errored is true if the Changes information is incomplete because\\n100: \\t// the planning operation failed. An errored plan cannot be applied,\\n101: \\t// but can be cautiously inspected for debugging purposes.\\n102: \\tErrored bool\\n103: \\n104: \\t// Checks captures a snapshot of the (probably-incomplete) check results\\n105: \\t// at the end of the planning process.\\n106: \\t//\\n107: \\t// If this plan is applyable (that is, if the planning process completed\\n108: \\t// without errors) then the set of checks here should be complete even\\n109: \\t// though some of them will likely have StatusUnknown where the check\\n110: \\t// condition depends on values we won't know until the apply step.\\n111: \\tChecks *states.CheckResults\\n112: \\n113: \\t// RelevantAttributes is a set of resource instance addresses and\\n114: \\t// attributes that are either directly affected by proposed changes or may\\n115: \\t// have indirectly contributed to them via references in expressions.\\n116: \\t//\\n117: \\t// This is the result of a heuristic and is intended only as a hint to\\n118: \\t// the UI layer in case it wants to emphasize or de-emphasize certain\\n119: \\t// resources. Don't use this to drive any non-cosmetic behavior, especially\\n120: \\t// including anything that would be subject to compatibility constraints.\\n121: \\tRelevantAttributes []globalref.ResourceAttr\\n122: \\n123: \\t// PrevRunState and PriorState both describe the situation that the plan\\n124: \\t// was derived from:\\n125: \\t//\\n126: \\t// PrevRunState is a representation of the outcome of the previous\\n127: \\t// Terraform operation, without any updates from the remote system but\\n128: \\t// potentially including some changes that resulted from state upgrade\\n129: \\t// actions.\\n130: \\t//\\n131: \\t// PriorState is a representation of the current state of remote objects,\\n132: \\t// which will differ from PrevRunState if the \\\"refresh\\\" step returned\\n133: \\t// different data, which might reflect drift.\\n134: \\t//\\n135: \\t// PriorState is the main snapshot we use for actions during apply.\\n136: \\t// PrevRunState is only here so that we can diff PriorState against it in\\n137: \\t// order to report to the user any out-of-band changes we've detected.\\n138: \\tPrevRunState *states.State\\n139: \\tPriorState   *states.State\\n140: \\n141: \\t// ExternalReferences are references that are being made to resources within\\n142: \\t// the plan from external sources.\\n143: \\t//\\n144: \\t// This is never recorded outside of Terraform. It is not written into the\\n145: \\t// binary plan file, and it is not written into the JSON structured outputs.\\n146: \\t// The testing framework never writes the plans out but holds everything in\\n147: \\t// memory as it executes, so there is no need to add any kind of\\n148: \\t// serialization for this field. This does mean that you shouldn't rely on\\n149: \\t// this field existing unless you have just generated the plan.\\n150: \\tExternalReferences []*addrs.Reference\\n151: \\n152: \\t// Overrides contains the set of overrides that were applied while making\\n153: \\t// this plan. We need to provide the same set of overrides when applying\\n154: \\t// the plan so we preserve them here. As with  ExternalReferences, this is\\n155: \\t// only used by the testing framework and so isn't written into any external\\n156: \\t// representation of the plan.\\n157: \\tOverrides *mocking.Overrides\\n158: \\n159: \\t// Timestamp is the record of truth for when the plan happened.\\n160: \\tTimestamp time.Time\\n161: \\n162: \\t// ProviderFunctionResults stores hashed results from all provider\\n163: \\t// function calls, so that calls during apply can be checked for\\n164: \\t// consistency.\\n165: \\tProviderFunctionResults []providers.FunctionHash\\n166: }\\n167: \\n168: // ProviderAddrs returns a list of all of the provider configuration addresses\\n169: // referenced throughout the receiving plan.\\n170: //\\n171: // The result is de-duplicated so that each distinct address appears only once.\\n172: func (p *Plan) ProviderAddrs() []addrs.AbsProviderConfig {\\n173: \\tif p == nil || p.Changes == nil {\\n174: \\t\\treturn nil\\n175: \\t}\\n176: \\n177: \\tm := map[string]addrs.AbsProviderConfig{}\\n178: \\tfor _, rc := range p.Changes.Resources {\\n179: \\t\\tm[rc.ProviderAddr.String()] = rc.ProviderAddr\\n180: \\t}\\n181: \\tif len(m) == 0 {\\n182: \\t\\treturn nil\\n183: \\t}\\n184: \\n185: \\t// This is mainly just so we'll get stable results for testing purposes.\\n186: \\tkeys := make([]string, 0, len(m))\\n187: \\tfor k := range m {\\n188: \\t\\tkeys = append(keys, k)\\n189: \\t}\\n190: \\tsort.Strings(keys)\\n191: \\n192: \\tret := make([]addrs.AbsProviderConfig, len(keys))\\n193: \\tfor i, key := range keys {\\n194: \\t\\tret[i] = m[key]\\n195: \\t}\\n196: \\n197: \\treturn ret\\n198: }\\n199: \\n200: // Backend represents the backend-related configuration and other data as it\\n201: // existed when a plan was created.\\n202: type Backend struct {\\n203: \\t// Type is the type of backend that the plan will apply against.\\n204: \\tType string\\n205: \\n206: \\t// Config is the configuration of the backend, whose schema is decided by\\n207: \\t// the backend Type.\\n208: \\tConfig DynamicValue\\n209: \\n210: \\t// Workspace is the name of the workspace that was active when the plan\\n211: \\t// was created. It is illegal to apply a plan created for one workspace\\n212: \\t// to the state of another workspace.\\n213: \\t// (This constraint is already enforced by the statefile lineage mechanism,\\n214: \\t// but storing this explicitly allows us to return a better error message\\n215: \\t// in the situation where the user has the wrong workspace selected.)\\n216: \\tWorkspace string\\n217: }\\n218: CompactDiffFormatter produces a condensed, summary-style diff output for\n// terraform plan, showing only resource-level changes without attribute-level\n// detail.\ntype CompactDiffFormatter struct{}\n\n// Format returns a compact summary of planned changes grouped by action type.\n// Each resource change is shown as a single line with its action and address.\nfunc (f *CompactDiffFormatter) Format(plan *plans.Plan, schemas *schemarepo.Schemas) string {\n\tif plan == nil || plan.Changes == nil {\n\t\treturn \"\"\n\t}\n\n\t// Group resources by action\n\tactionGroups := make(map[plans.Action][]string)\n\n\t// Collect all resource changes\n\tfor _, rc := range plan.Changes.Resources {\n\t\t// Skip deposed resources\n\t\tif rc.DeposedKey != \"\" {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\taction := rc.Action\n\t\taddr := rc.Addr.String()\n\t\tactionGroups[action] = append(actionGroups[action], addr)\n\t}\n\n\t// Sort addresses within each action group for consistent output\n\tfor _, addresses := range actionGroups {\n\t\tsort.Strings(addresses)\n\t}\n\n\t// Define the order of actions for display\n\tactionOrder := []plans.Action{\n\t\tplans.Create,\n\t\tplans.Update,\n\t\tplans.Delete,\n\t\tplans.DeleteThenCreate,\n\t\tplans.CreateThenDelete,\n\t\tplans.Read,\n\t\tplans.CreateThenForget,\n\t\tplans.Forget,\n\t\tplans.NoOp,\n\t}\n\n\tvar buf bytes.Buffer\n\n\t// Write resources grouped by action in the defined order\n\tfor _, action := range actionOrder {\n\t\taddresses, ok := actionGroups[action]\n\t\tif !ok || len(addresses) == 0 {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// Write action header\n\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"# %s\\n\", actionToString(action))\n\n\t\t// Write each resource\n\t\tfor _, addr := range addresses {\n\t\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s %s\\n\", actionSymbol(action), addr)\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tbuf.WriteString(\"\\n\")\n\t}\n\n\t// Write summary counts\n\tsummary := f.summarizeCounts(actionGroups)\n\tif summary != \"\" {\n\t\tfmt.Fprintf(&buf, \"%s\\n\", summary)\n\t}\n\n\treturn buf.String()\n}\n\n// actionSymbol returns a short symbol representation of an action\nfunc actionSymbol(action plans.Action) string {\n\tswitch action {\n\tcase plans.Create:\n\t\treturn \"+\"\n\tcase plans.Update:\n\t\treturn \"~\"\n\tcase plans.Delete:\n\t\treturn \"-\"\n\tcase plans.DeleteThenCreate:\n\t\treturn \"±\"\n\tcase plans.CreateThenDelete:\n\t\treturn \"∓\"\n\tcase plans.Read:\n\t\treturn \"<=\"\n\tcase plans.Forget:\n\t\treturn \".\"\n\tcase plans.CreateThenForget:\n\t\treturn \"±\"\n\tcase plans.NoOp:\n\t\treturn \" \"\n\tdefault:\n\t\treturn \"?\"\n\t}\n}\n\n// actionToString returns a human-readable string for an action\nfunc actionToString(action plans.Action) string {\n\tswitch action {\n\tcase plans.Create:\n\t\treturn \"Create\"\n\tcase plans.Update:\n\t\treturn \"Update\"\n\tcase plans.Delete:\n\t\treturn \"Delete\"\n\tcase plans.DeleteThenCreate:\n\t\treturn \"Replace\"\n\tcase plans.CreateThenDelete:\n\t\treturn \"Replace\"\n\tcase plans.Read:\n\t\treturn \"Read\"\n\tcase plans.Forget:\n\t\treturn summary line with counts of each action type\nfunc (f *CompactDiffFormatter) summarizeCounts(groups map[plans.Action][]string) string {\n\tcreates := len(groups[plans.Create])\n\tupdates :=
